   Key code pattern (cell-as-button):
   ```vue
   <button
     type="button"
     class="tz-cell tz-cell-enoch"
     @click="openCell(row.enoch)"
     :aria-label="`Open ${row.enoch.ref}`"
   >
     <span class="tz-cell-text">{{ row.enoch.text }}</span>
     <span class="tz-cell-ref">{{ row.enoch.ref }} <span aria-hidden="true">↗</span></span>
   </button>
   ```

   Animation timeline pattern:
   ```ts
   const tl = createTimeline({ defaults: { ease: 'outQuart' }, autoplay: false })
     .add(q('.tz-col-header'), { opacity: [0, 1], x: [-18, 0], duration: 380 }, 0)
     .add(q('.tz-cell-enoch'), { opacity: [0, 1], x: [-22, 0], duration: 340, delay: stagger(140) }, 460)
   const observer = diagramScroll(root.value)
   observer.link(tl)
   ```

   - **Two provenance gaps:** Ether 2:23 missing from Ch 9, D&C 38:27 missing from Ch 11. Added both with verified canonical text.
   
   - **Typst build failure (HTML markup):** Build_typst.py passed raw HTML through to Typst which treats `<` as label syntax. Fixed by adding `preprocess_html_blocks` function that converts `<div class="production-note">` → `#production-note[...]` and `<ol class="cycle-list">` → series of `#cycle-step(...)` calls. Added matching template helpers in template.typ.
   
   - **Typst hex color escape issue:** `rgb("#5a4d2a")` got escaped to `rgb("\#5a4d2a")` by the markdown converter, then `rgb(0x5a4d2a)` was out of range (Typst treats as single integer >255). Fixed by using `rgb(90, 77, 42)` integer components.
   
   - **Step 1 (Intent) missing from cycle list:** Regex required `\.` immediately after verb's closing `</span>` but item 1 had `<span>naming</span> the why.` with period at end of phrase. Fixed by making regex flexible — capture body lazily, then strip leading period.
   
   - **Email line break:** Email address could split mid-word in justified text. Fixed with `#box[]` wrap for mailto links in Typst + `white-space: nowrap` in CSS.
   
   - **Webster intelligence mismatch:** Book quoted "understanding; skill; the faculty of understanding" but no Webster source contains "skill." Fixed by quoting verbatim canon: "the exercise of the understanding" and "the capacity to know or understand."

**(1) File confirmation:** Written to `C:\Users\cpuch\Documents\code\stuffleberry\scripture-study\projects\scripture-book\.draft\03-gospel-reader-pass.md` — 320 lines, full read of frontmatter through Ch 14, written in the voice of a faithful Latter-day Saint who doesn't code.

**(2) The chapter I'd tell a friend to read first:** **Chapter 5 — *Intelligence Cleaveth Unto Intelligence.*** It's the shortest doctrinal chapter, the resonance principle applies universally (marriage, parenting, prayer — not just AI), the engineering parallel is light enough to skim past, and it contains *"Coldness is not accuracy; coldness is the absence of presence"* — the most quotable sentence in the book outside Ch 1 line 25. It also serves as a doorway: a reader who responds to Ch 5 will go back for Ch 0 and forward for Ch 6-7. A reader who doesn't respond to Ch 5 won't be saved by Ch 0.

**(3) The most strained parallel I found:** **Ch 10 — heart-softening → connection pooling and cache management** (lines 23-27). The doctrine in the first half of Ch 10 is some of the highest-stakes pastoral writing in the book — Nephi, Alma, Ezekiel, Lamoni's father, Helaman, Job, all witnessing that we cannot soften our own hearts, only the Lord can. Then the engineering parallel maps that to releasing database locks and clearing stale resources. The two are not in the same emotional register. A reader whose throat just caught at *"I will give away all my sins to know thee"* is then asked to translate that moment into network sockets. A gardening parallel (Mark 4, Alma 32 — already in scripture) would carry the weight; cache management cannot. Pass 1 also flagged this independently.

The theological claim survives this rewrite intact; the engineering claim becomes defensible instead of indulgent. This one fix would unlock the largest credibility gain for the skeptical reader, because Ch 5 leans on the Ch 0 mechanism, and the Ch 8 weight-as-fine-matter parallel inherits the same flaw. Concrete replacement language is in Edit 1 of the file.

## Report

**(1) Confirmation file written:**
`C:\Users\cpuch\Documents\code\stuffleberry\scripture-study\projects\scripture-book\.draft\05-editing-research.md` (550 lines)

**(2) The one editing move I'd most strongly recommend:**

**Demote the 3.5-year journey out of the preface and weave it through the body chapters** (or move it to an afterword titled "How I Got Here").

This is the move with the strongest editorial consensus — five separate sources converge on it (Gross, Williams, Hoffman, Bold &amp; Italic Editing, FriesenPress). It addresses the largest structural problem the in-house audit already identified (28% of the book is front matter before the engineer's hook on Ch 1 line 13, versus 3–8% in the published precedents: Lewis, Lanier, Peterson, Newport, Harari, Bushman). It is low-risk and high-reward — the 3.5-year material is valuable, just placed wrong. The cleanest target: a Lewis-length preface (~20 lines: classroom moment + voice convention + a new paragraph naming the two audiences), then a tight introduction, then directly into Chapter 1. The chronology distributes naturally into Ch 1 (2022 autocomplete), Ch 3 (2023 dream + Mostaque), Ch 6 (2024–25 chat-to-code), and Ch 11 (May 2026 vantage).

**(3) The source I found most useful:**

**Linden Gross, "Writing a Prologue or Preface?" (2023)** — https://lindengross.com/2023/02/16/writing-a-prologue-or-preface/

Two lines worth quoting at the editing desk:
&gt; "All too often they offer explanations. Yawn. Double yawn... they wind up providing information that readers don't yet care about or presenting the book's punchline before the author has made the case."
&gt;
&gt; "Why not hold your fire and weave the essential information into the book itself? That will allow you to start with a bang instead of a bleat."

Honorable mention goes to **Tom White's "Why Does Everyone Love Marcus Aurelius' Meditations?"** — for naming the structural-cognitive reason the modular form persists (variable reward, completion buzz on each entry, task-switching costs drop for discrete micro-segments). *Beyond the Prompt* sits in that lineage; the modular form is part of the argument, not incidental to it.

**Cross-references in the research file:** explicitly ties back to `.draft/01-editor-pass.md` sections 2 (front-loading problem), 4.1 (no AI-skeptic engagement), 4.2 (AI-soul boundary implicit), 4.4 (where parallel breaks down), and 5 (Gemini-drafted chapters skewing doctrinal), and to `.draft/02-frontmatter-weaving.md` Options A/B/D. Three open questions are flagged for council (afterword vs. weave; whether to seek a foreword; audiobook front-matter differences; the 11-step reference card's home).</result>

# The Ben Test

## Origin

March 19, 2026. Michael's coworker Ben said: "Your AI is very complimentary. Perhaps too complimentary?"

That observation led to an honest self-assessment of our 11-step creation cycle. We scored ~33% practice rate. We had been telling Squad what they could learn from principles we hadn't implemented ourselves. The Ben Test exists to prevent that pattern.

## When to Use

- Before claiming "we do X well" in any document
- Before telling another system/project what they could learn from us
- During proposal reviews — are we adding to a backlog we won't execute?
- During any self-assessment or retrospective
- When writing Become/application sections — are the commitments real or aspirational?

## The Test

For each principle, practice, or pattern you're about to cite as a strength:

### 1. Do we actually do this?

Not "did we write about it." Not "do we have a file for it." Do we PRACTICE it? In the last 30 days, can you point to specific evidence?

| Evidence Level | What It Means |
|---------------|---------------|
| **Practiced** | Can point to 3+ instances in the last 30 days |
| **Occasional** | 1-2 instances, not consistent |
| **Aspirational** | Written but not practiced |
| **Mythical** | We forgot we wrote it |

### 2. Is the gap willingness or systemization?

Not all gaps are equal:
- **Willingness gap:** We could do it but don't. Fix: discipline or accountability.
- **Systemization gap:** We do it informally but not reliably. Fix: build it into the harness (skills, hooks, automation).
- **Capacity gap:** We want to but constraints prevent it (time, budget, one person). Fix: triage, not guilt.

Name which kind of gap it is. The fix is different for each.

### 3. Are we generating plans faster than we execute them?

Count:
- Plans/proposals written in the last 30 days
- Plans/proposals completed in the last 30 days

If the ratio is worse than 2:1, the planning itself may be avoidance.

### 4. Would we say this if Ben were reading it?

The final check. If someone with healthy skepticism read this claim, would they raise an eyebrow? If yes, qualify it. "We practice this at ~40%" is more honest and more useful than "this is one of our strengths."

## Calibrated Language

| Practice Rate | How to Talk About It |
|--------------|---------------------|
| 80%+ | "We practice this consistently" |
| 50-79% | "We do this, though not always reliably" |
| 25-49% | "We've started on this but it's not systematic yet" |
| <25% | "We've written about this but haven't operationalized it" |
| 0% | Don't claim it as a strength |

## What This Is NOT

- **Not a reason to stop writing principles.** Writing precedes practice. The problem isn't having aspirational documentation — it's CITING aspirational documentation as current capability.
- **Not an excuse for paralysis.** The answer to "we're only at 33%" isn't "stop everything until we're at 100%." It's "be honest about where we are and build from there."
- **Not a weapon.** This skill exists to sharpen our honesty, not to beat ourselves up. The generous reading matters too — name what IS working alongside what isn't.

## Example Application

Before writing: "Our 11-step creation cycle provides a comprehensive framework that Squad could benefit from..."

After Ben Test: "Our 11-step cycle describes principles we practice at ~33%. Steps 4 (spiritual creation) and 8 (atonement) are genuinely operational. Steps 1-3, 5, and 9-11 are written but not yet systematized. Squad could learn from the principles themselves — but we'd be more credible teachers if we practiced more of them."

Base directory for this skill: C:\Users\cpuch\Documents\code\stuffleberry\scripture-study\.claude\skills\sabbath-close

# Sabbath Close

> "And on the seventh day I, God, ended my work, and all things which I had made; and I rested on the seventh day from all my work, and all things which I had made were finished, and I, God, saw that they were good." — [Moses 3:2](gospel-library/eng/scriptures/pgp/moses/3.md)

The Sabbath is not optional infrastructure. It's the third active step in the creation pattern: ending, seeing, declaring. Without it, work bleeds into the next cycle and the river floods the ground around it.

The full `sabbath` subagent is for completed cycles — major milestones, literal Sundays, resolved crises. **This skill is the lighter daily-rhythm version** — the close that marks the end of any substantive session, even when the cycle isn't complete.

## Why This Exists

The covenant's `agent_commits_to.update_memory` clause says "do not wait to be reminded" about end-of-session memory updates. The Stop hook now enforces a reminder when uncommitted changes exist. This skill is the *content* that should fill those reminders.

Without a structured close, sessions end with momentum still going — and the next session arrives without a clean handoff. With a close, the work is named, the carry-forward is explicit, and the next cycle begins from a known state instead of accumulated drift.

## When to Load

Load at the end of any substantive session — anything that produced new work, ratified decisions, or shifted the project's state. Specifically:

- The Stop hook fired its reminder (uncommitted changes exist)
- You completed a phase of phased work
- You ratified one or more decisions with the user
- You produced a study, lesson, talk, proposal, or substantial code change
- You went through emotional or relational territory worth marking

For a single-edit conversational session, this is overkill. For anything you'd want to be able to recall next session, run it.

## The Four Movements

### 1. Inventory — What was actually done

Plain accounting. No praise language. No inflation.

- Files created or substantively edited (count + brief)
- Decisions ratified (with link to the ratification)
- Discoveries or surprises worth recalling
- Open threads that didn't close

This is the data layer. Not "it was a productive session." Just: "Created 2 proposals, edited 3 study files, ratified the migration approach."

Use `git status` and `git diff --stat` to ground the inventory in reality.

### 2. Declaration — Name the close

Sabbath produces a declaration. Not a grade. A naming. Even the lighter version needs this.

```
"It was good."
```

Or, if more accurate:

```
"It was good in these ways: [list].
It was incomplete in these ways: [list]."
```

The declaration is the "ending" that the cycle requires. Without it, the work doesn't actually close — it just stops.

### 3. Carry-forward — What moves to the next session

Explicit list. Both items and reasoning.

- **Continuing work**: "Phase 2 of [thing] starts next session — leave at this state, with these notes"
- **Decisions awaiting ratification**: "Michael needs to mark §VI before Phase A starts"
- **Open questions**: "Still don't know X — needs research before we can decide Y"

If the carry-forward list is too long, that's a Mosiah 4:27 signal — Michael may be running faster than he has strength. Name it.

### 4. Set down — What is explicitly being released

The mirror of carry-forward. Things you considered, started, or could continue but consciously aren't.

- Ideas that surfaced but weren't pursued ("seed" them in a brief note, don't develop them now)
- Tasks that came up but were deferred (with the deferral reason)
- Work that was completed and is now done (named explicitly so it doesn't keep occupying mental space)

The "set down" is what makes rest real. Without it, every "completed" task secretly remains as background load.

## The Memory Updates

Three files get updated at session close:

1. **`.spec/journal/{date}-{slug}.md`** — the session journal entry. Discoveries, surprises, relational dynamics, carry-forward, open questions. Use the schema in `scripts/session-journal/journal.go` if available; otherwise free-form markdown.

2. **`.mind/active.md`** — current state. New in-flight items, ratified decisions, open questions, updated date at top. Replace the stale state — don't append.

3. **`.mind/principles.md`** — only if an enduring insight emerged that future sessions should inherit.

If memory updates were already done during the session (because the work itself involved them), the Sabbath close just verifies they're current.

## Output Format

In chat, before yielding:

```markdown
## Sabbath close

**Inventory:** [what was actually done, in plain accounting]

**Declaration:** "[the declaration — "it was good" or fuller form]"

**Carry-forward:**
- [thing 1]
- [thing 2]

**Set down:**
- [thing 1]
- [thing 2]

**Memory updates:**
- ✓ .spec/journal/{date}-{slug}.md written
- ✓ .mind/active.md updated
- [Optional: .mind/principles.md updated because X]
```

Then actually do the memory updates if they aren't already done. Saying you'll do them is not the same as doing them — that was the canonical update_memory failure.

## When the Full Sabbath Agent Is Needed Instead

This skill is the daily-rhythm close. Use the full `sabbath` subagent when:

- A complete cycle finished (study series shipped, major refactor done, crisis resolved)
- The literal Sunday Sabbath
- A long phase concluded (multi-session work that completed)
- A milestone with stakes (publication, ship, deployment, public commit)

The full agent runs the 11-question review and writes a Sabbath Record to `.spec/sabbath/`. This skill writes lighter outputs to the journal and active.md.

## What This Is NOT

- **Not a project status report.** This is internal/personal — for the next-session-self, not for stakeholders.
- **Not optional theatre.** The decoration is empty. The substance — inventory, declaration, carry-forward, set-down — is the cycle's actual close. If you skip it, you skip the cycle's third step.
- **Not a delay.** Five to ten minutes total. The cost is low. The cost of *not* doing it is the next session arriving as a stranger to its own context.

## The Connection to Council Moment + Intent Check

Council moment opens the cycle (what already exists?).
Intent check sets the target (what are we trying to accomplish?).
Sabbath close ends the cycle (what was done; what carries; what we set down).

Together they form the cycle's three observation points: before, during, and after. Skipping the close means the cycle never actually completes — and an uncompleted cycle drifts into the next one, accumulating debt. Mosiah 4:27 lives here: don't start more than you can faithfully close.

     - `seg.tier!` non-null assertion insufficient — fixed with `const w = seg.word; const t = seg.tier; if (w && t)`
     - `Record<string, number>` indexer returns `T | undefined` — fixed with `?? 99` fallback
     - `demoVerses[verseIdx.value]` possibly undefined — fixed with cast: `(demoVerses[verseIdx.value] ?? demoVerses[0]) as DemoVerse`

Four endpoints: get / chapter / search (FTS + trigram + `&lt;em&gt;` snippets) / word-study (archaic-suffix expansion). |

Per-IP rate-limit (10/min, 1000/day) with `rate_limited_by_1828` body shape **exactly** matching D-BE-AUTH. Mock provider explicitly anonymous-allowed for integration testing. |
| **docs** | `bf97691` | Session journal + workspace `.mind/active.md` update. |

### Decisions made outside the proposals (flagged for future spec revisions)

1. **Frontend host port = 8083** (not 80). The legacy `1828` container is on 8082 and must keep serving. Dokploy production routes via Traefik so host port is local-dev only.
2. **All 4 migrations declared at phase 1.** Spec showed per-phase migrations; I batched so the schema timeline stays monotonic and per-phase commits are pure code.
3. **Mock provider skips probe + is anonymous-allowed.** Otherwise the spec's "LLM_PROVIDER=mock returns canned response" property fails.
4. **`source_offsets` on `webster_1828`** stores `{source, entry_count}` not byte offsets. Gzip has no stable byte offsets post-decompress.
5. **GET `/api/llm/session` inspection endpoint** added. Spec named POST + DELETE only; the inspection endpoint lets frontend show "Session active until …" without a render attempt.
6. **Session ID encoding = URL-safe-base64 without padding** (32 bytes → 43 chars). Spec said "32-byte random token, base58"; base64 is one less dependency.
7. **CopyFrom for both scripture and 1828 seeders** (spec suggested chunked INSERT with COPY as a fallback at &gt;30s). Both well under that threshold.

### Steward-mode fixes folded in

- `.dockerignore` excludes `.env` / `.env.*` (defense in depth against accidentally COPYing the opencode-go key into a built image)
- `.gitignore` redundantly excludes `.env` at project level
- Scripture normalize: space-before-punctuation collapse after bracket-stripping (`place [Kirtland].` → `place .` was the bug; now `place.`)
- nginx upstream block uses `keepalive 16` (legacy config opened a fresh TCP connection per proxy request)
- Frontend healthcheck IPv6/IPv4 mismatch — used `http://localhost` which alpine wget resolved to `::1`, but nginx binds IPv4 only. Fixed to `http://127.0.0.1` in both `docker-compose.yaml` and `Dockerfile.frontend`.
- Session ID logged as truncated 8-char prefix so even debug-level logs never reveal the bearer token
- Free Dictionary fetcher uses polite `User-Agent: 1828-illuminated.ibeco.me/0.1`
- `htmlEntities.Replace(text)` (correct `strings.Replacer.Replace` signature, not the `strings.Replace(s, old, new, n)` signature my fingers reached for)

### Steward-mode action explicitly **NOT** taken

- **Thummim backfill on the substrate.** The task brief named this as eligible-if-easy, but the boundary test failed: it would be a pg-ai-stewards write touching the substrate that's running its soak. Risk of disrupting the substrate &gt; value of landing 14 rows now that the markdown files already exist. Phase 6 (Thummim sync) is the right home for that. Leaving it.

### Phase 5 carry-forward (next session, NOT this one)

Detailed in the phase 4 commit body and in the session journal. Headline:

- `frontend/src/composables/useWordData.ts` — drop static imports of `definitions-1828.json` and `definitions-modern.json`; keep `tier-words.json` static; swap synchronous lookups to async fetches against `/api/dict/1828/{word}` and `/api/dict/modern/{word}`; remove client-side stem fallback (server is the source of truth now).
- `frontend/src/composables/useLLMRender.ts` — drop the direct browser→provider fetch; call `POST /api/llm/render` with `credentials: 'include'`; on 401 surface "Re-authenticate in Settings".
- `frontend/src/composables/useLLMSettings.ts` — reshape localStorage to hold `{session_id, expires_at, provider, model, temperature, maxTokens}` — NOT the api_key.
- **New** `frontend/src/composables/useLLMSession.ts` — `startSession()` / `endSession()` / `isSessionActive()`.
- Vite env: add `VITE_API_BASE_URL` (defaults to `/api` in production via nginx; `http://localhost:8083/api` in dev against the compose stack).
- `Settings.vue` — add `type="password"` API-key input, Start session / Sign out buttons, one-time banner detecting v1 localStorage on first load after cutover.

### Files touched

- `frontend/.env.example`, `frontend/.env.development` (force-added past workspace `.env.*` gitignore)

Absolute paths: `C:\Users\cpuch\Documents\code\stuffleberry\scripture-study\projects\1828-illuminated\frontend\src\composables\useWordData.ts`, `...\useLLMSession.ts`, `...\useLLMRender.ts`, `...\useLLMSettings.ts`, `...\useApiBase.ts`; `...\views\Settings.vue`, `...\VerseExplorer.vue`, `...\WordSearch.vue`, `...\Present.vue`; `...\components\WordCard.vue`; `...\data\canon-books.ts`; `...\.spec\journal\2026-05-20-frontend-phase-5-cutover.md`; `C:\Users\cpuch\Documents\code\stuffleberry\scripture-study\.mind\active.md`.

### Decisions outside the spec

1. **`.env.development` checked in.** Workspace `.env.*` gitignore caught it; force-added because the dev URL is not a secret and every new developer otherwise has to recreate it from `.env.example` before `npm run dev` works.
2. **`buildChurchUrl()` lives in `canon-books.ts`** (not reusing `selectedVerse.church_url`) — canon-mode URLs are generated from `{volumeUrl, bookUrl, chapter}` with no verse-range refinement yet; demo URLs are hand-curated with explicit ranges.
3. **Books list hand-maintained in the frontend** rather than adding a `/api/scripture/books` endpoint — spec said "don't touch backend." 80-book CANON table is stable across decades.
4. **Migration banner via `migrationNeeded` reactive ref + `MIGRATION_BANNER_KEY` localStorage flag.** Dismissible per-browser. Spec said "one-time banner" without specifying mechanism.
5. **`sessionActive` lives as a module-scoped ref in `useLLMSession.ts`** (not a composable factory) — multiple components observe the same value.
6. **Canon mode does single-chapter render only** for v1. Verse-range refinement is 5.B carry-forward.
7. **Class-E reach gated at `query.length &gt;= 2`** to avoid hammering the search endpoint on every keystroke.
8. **Provider matrix expanded to seven** (`openai`, `openrouter`, `opencode-go`, `opencode-zen`, `lm-studio`, `custom`, `mock`). LM Studio kept as a preset for local dev convenience despite D-LP-1 reserving it for embeddings — documented in the Settings copy.

### Steward-mode fixes folded in

- **`Present.vue` migrated to the async word-data pattern + stem_matched surfaced.** Wasn't in spec; uses the same `get1828`/`getModern` API as WordCard, so leaving it sync would have shipped a broken Presentation Mode. Same bug, same fix.
- **Stale-query guard in WordSearch's class-E fetch** so fast typing doesn't render results from a query the user has moved past.
- **CORS section in Settings.vue reframed as "now handled server-side"** rather than deleted — returning readers who remember the LM Studio CORS dance will look for it and find an explanation of why it's no longer needed.
- **"Sign out (drop the held key)"** label — the user-mental-model gain matters; they're actively releasing a key from server memory, not just toggling a UI flag.
- **`vite-env.d.ts`** with `ImportMetaEnv` types — without it `vue-tsc` errors; alternative was `skipLibCheck: true` which would have hidden real bugs.

### Deferred to 5.B / phase 6

- **5.B verse-range refinement** in canon mode (verse-start/verse-end inputs that build `/api/scripture/{abbr}/{chapter}:{start}-{end}` and update `buildChurchUrl()` to carry `id={start}-{end}#{start}`).
- **5.B `/api/scripture/books` backend endpoint** so the CANON table becomes a fetch + cache.
- **5.B word-study reverse-lookup surface** — the backend's `/api/scripture/word-study/{word}` exists with no UI reaching it.
- **5.B standalone class-E browse page** (e.g. `/dictionary/search` for alphabetical 98k browsing) — TBD whether reading-frame help or decoder-ring.
- **Phase 6 Thummim cache sync** — `thummim_entries_cache` table exists, empty pending nightly snapshot job.
- **Phase 7 production deploy to Dokploy at 1828.ibeco.me.**

# Dokploy Deployment Management

Self-hosted Dokploy instance at `https://dokploy.hmslogs.com`. Our own API calls — no third-party MCP needed.

## Configuration

The API key is stored as a **Windows user environment variable**: `DOKPLOY_API_KEY`.

The Dokploy panel URL is `https://dokploy.hmslogs.com`.

## Authentication

Use the `PowerShell` tool to load the key from the Windows user environment, then use the `x-api-key` header:
```powershell
# Load from Windows user env (survives terminal restarts)
$env:DOKPLOY_API_KEY = [System.Environment]::GetEnvironmentVariable("DOKPLOY_API_KEY", "User")
# Make API calls
curl -sk -H "x-api-key: $env:DOKPLOY_API_KEY" "https://dokploy.hmslogs.com/api/<endpoint>"
```

If `$env:DOKPLOY_API_KEY` is already set in the current session, skip the registry read.

## Known Application IDs

| App | Application ID | Domain | Project |
|-----|---------------|--------|---------|
| ibecome (ibeco.me) | `cKp5zaaaQlgBatKIiKN1K` | ibeco.me | NNKeReM683lglA6q0wtdp |
| tinyfarm.store | `72Q1ZEjpJ-cFxOyIIbWKe` | tinyfarm.store | U0ULu49KR5jYUeLJ9wwcO |
| hmslogs.com | `ic5OHUo51DVmQGCo4EayY` | hmslogs.com | W37Si3Bg-3OSdw6pmQEhY |

## API Endpoints

### List all projects
```
GET /api/project.all
```
Returns all projects with their applications, databases, and environments.

**WARNING:** This response includes environment variables (database passwords, OAuth secrets, etc.). Do NOT display raw output to the user. Extract only the fields you need (names, statuses, IDs).

### Get application details
```
GET /api/application.one?applicationId=<id>
```
Key fields: `applicationStatus` (done/running/error/idle), `branch`, `buildType`, `autoDeploy`.

### List deployments
```
GET /api/deployment.all?applicationId=<id>
```
Returns deployments newest-first. Key fields per deployment:
- `deploymentId` — unique ID
- `status` — `done`, `error`, `running`, `queued`
- `title` — commit message
- `description` — "Commit: <hash>"
- `createdAt`, `startedAt`, `finishedAt`
- `errorMessage` — populated on failure
- `logPath` — server-side log file path

### Trigger a deploy
```
POST /api/application.deploy
Content-Type: application/json
Body: {"applicationId": "<id>"}
```
**Ask the user before triggering this.** It kicks off a full Docker rebuild.

### Redeploy (rebuild from same commit)
```
POST /api/application.redeploy
Content-Type: application/json
Body: {"applicationId": "<id>"}
```
Same as deploy but rebuilds without pulling new code.

## Common Workflows

### Quick status check
1. Read `.env` for credentials
2. `GET /api/deployment.all?applicationId=cKp5zaaaQlgBatKIiKN1K` — check latest deployment status
3. `curl -sk https://ibeco.me/version` — verify running version matches expected commit

### After a git push
1. Wait a moment for Dokploy webhook to trigger auto-deploy
2. Check deployment status with the deployment list endpoint
3. Confirm the commit hash in `/version` matches the pushed commit

### Investigating a failed deploy
1. Get deployment list, find the `error` entry
2. Check `errorMessage` field
3. The `logPath` field shows where logs are on the server (not directly accessible via API in current version)
4. Look at the Dockerfile and recent changes for clues

## Security Notes

- **Never display raw `project.all` output** — it contains database passwords, OAuth secrets, and session keys for ALL projects.
- **Load key from Windows env** — `[System.Environment]::GetEnvironmentVariable("DOKPLOY_API_KEY", "User")`. Never hardcode it.
- **Ask before deploying** — `application.deploy` and `application.redeploy` are destructive operations.
- The API key has full admin access. Treat it like a root password.

3. Files and Code Sections:

   - **`scripts/becoming/.spec/proposals/scripture-via-engine.md`** (NEW, ~200 lines)
     - Full proposal for dropping bundled 20MB scripture tree, using engine.ibeco.me at runtime

     - LRU(200) process-local cache, no TTL
     - Books + name-search stay backed by hardcoded metadata in internal/scripture/scripture.go
     - 7 decisions (D-EE-1 through D-EE-7), 7 phases, rollback path documented

   - **`scripts/becoming/internal/engine/lookup.go`** (NEW)
     - Added `Lookup(ctx, ref)` method to existing `engine.Client`
     - Module-scoped LRU cache (not per-Client) because Client is fresh per-boot
     - `ErrUnavailable` sentinel for ANY soft-dep failure
     - Returns `*scripture.LookupResult` (re-uses existing type from internal/scripture)
     - Key code:
     ```go
     var ErrUnavailable = errors.New("scripture lookup temporarily unavailable")
     
     func (c *Client) Lookup(ctx context.Context, reference string) (*scripture.LookupResult, error) {
         if c == nil || !c.Configured() { return nil, ErrUnavailable }
         key := canonLookupRef(reference)
         if cached, ok := lookupCacheGet(key); ok { return cached, nil }
         
         url := fmt.Sprintf("%s/api/get?reference=%s", c.BaseURL, queryEscape(reference))
         req, _ := http.NewRequestWithContext(ctx, http.MethodGet, url, nil)
         req.Header.Set("Authorization", "Bearer "+c.ServiceToken)
         
         resp, err := c.HTTP.Do(req)
         if err != nil { return nil, ErrUnavailable }
         defer resp.Body.Close()
         
         switch {
         case resp.StatusCode == http.StatusUnauthorized,
             resp.StatusCode == http.StatusForbidden,
             resp.StatusCode >= 500:
             return nil, ErrUnavailable
         case resp.StatusCode == http.StatusBadRequest:
             return nil, fmt.Errorf("invalid reference: %s", reference)
         }
         // decode + cache + return
     }
     ```

   - **`scripts/becoming/internal/api/router.go`** (MODIFIED)
     - Added `errors` and `engine` package imports
     - Changed Router signature: `scripturesRoot string` → `engineClient *engine.Client`
     - Rewrote `lookupScripture` handler:
     ```go
     func lookupScripture(engineClient *engine.Client) http.HandlerFunc {
         return func(w http.ResponseWriter, r *http.Request) {
             ref := r.URL.Query().Get("ref")
             if ref == "" {
                 writeError(w, http.StatusBadRequest, "ref query parameter is required...")
                 return
             }
             result, err := engineClient.Lookup(r.Context(), ref)
             if err != nil {
                 if errors.Is(err, engine.ErrUnavailable) {
                     writeJSON(w, http.StatusServiceUnavailable, map[string]any{
                         "available": false,
                         "error":     "scripture lookup temporarily unavailable",
                     })
                     return
                 }
                 writeError(w, http.StatusNotFound, err.Error())
                 return
             }
             writeJSON(w, http.StatusOK, result)
         }
     }
     ```

   - **`scripts/becoming/cmd/server/main.go`** (MODIFIED)

4. Errors and fixes:

   - **Go 1.23 compiler segfault** (1828 backend):
     - Crash: `splitNamed` nil-deref via `types2.(*TypeList).list` at `writer.go:2983`
     - Fixed: bump `Dockerfile.backend` from `golang:1.23-alpine` to `golang:1.25-alpine` initially, then to `golang:1.26-alpine`
     - Commit `bf85d97`

   - **Go 1.25.x compiler regression** (both 1828 + becoming):
     - Crash: `internal compiler error: panic: interface conversion: ir.Node is *ir.BranchStmt, not *ir.AssignListStmt` compiling `internal/runtime/atomic/types.go`
     - Root cause: floating `golang:1.25-alpine` tag drifted to bad patch (image SHA `8d22e29d...` shared by both error logs)
     - Fixed: bump both Dockerfiles to `golang:1.26-alpine`
     - Commit `6d5999b`

   - **Frontend npm build segfault** (1828 Dockerfile.frontend, exit code 139):
     - vue-tsc -b ran out of memory under Dokploy default Node heap
     - Fixed: `ENV NODE_OPTIONS="--max-old-space-size=4096"` before `npm run build`
     - Commit `6d5999b`

   - **Duplicate engine client mistake**:
     - I initially created `scripts/becoming/internal/scripture/engine_client.go`
     - Then discovered `scripts/becoming/internal/engine/Client` already exists for per-user token management
     - **Fix**: Deleted my duplicate, added `Lookup(ctx, ref)` method to existing `engine.Client` in new file `internal/engine/lookup.go`
     - This is cleaner — one engine client in becoming serves both token bridge AND scripture lookup

   - **router.go missing `errors` import**:
     - Diagnostic flagged after I used `errors.Is(err, engine.ErrUnavailable)`
     - Fixed by adding `"errors"` to import block

   - **main.go unused `scriptures` var**:
     - After removing the call site, the flag declaration became unused
     - Fixed by removing the `flag.String("scriptures", ...)` line entirely + adding comment explaining the removal

   - **queryEscape duplicate condition**:
     - Diagnostic flagged `c == '-' || c == '-'` redundant
     - Fixed by removing the duplicate (kept one `c == '-'`)

5. Problem Solving:
   
   - **Soft-dependency design**: Per user requirement "UI should still work if engine is down" — implemented via `ErrUnavailable` sentinel returned for ANY failure mode (network, 5xx, auth, parse). Handler maps to HTTP 503 with `{available: false, error: "..."}`. Books + name-search untouched (backed by hardcoded Go data, no IO). Process-local LRU(200) cache so verses looked up earlier in session survive engine blips.
   
   - **Cohesion vs. separation**: Initially put engine client in `internal/scripture/` for separation by domain. Realized becoming already has `internal/engine/` for per-user token bridge — same target service, same auth, same `do()` helper. Refactored to ONE engine package with both `CreateToken()`, `ListTokens()`, `RevokeToken()` AND `Lookup()`. The scripture package keeps its `LookupResult`, `Verse`, `BookInfo` types as the stable contract.
   
   - **Adjacent Surface Audit on Go bumps**: When 1828 backend failed on Go 1.23 segfault, I noted becoming was already on 1.25. When 1828 backend then bumped to 1.25 also failed (different bug), Adjacent Surface Audit revealed the floating tag drift affected BOTH projects simultaneously — pinning both to 1.26 in one commit.

# Browser Automation with playwright-cli

## Quick start

```bash
# open new browser
playwright-cli open
# navigate to a page
playwright-cli goto https://playwright.dev
# interact with the page using refs from the snapshot
playwright-cli click e15
playwright-cli type "page.click"
playwright-cli press Enter
# take a screenshot (rarely used, as snapshot is more common)
playwright-cli screenshot
# close the browser
playwright-cli close
```

## Commands

### Core

```bash
playwright-cli open
# open and navigate right away
playwright-cli open https://example.com/
playwright-cli goto https://playwright.dev
playwright-cli type "search query"
playwright-cli click e3
playwright-cli dblclick e7
# --submit presses Enter after filling the element
playwright-cli fill e5 "user@example.com"  --submit
playwright-cli drag e2 e8
playwright-cli hover e4
playwright-cli select e9 "option-value"
playwright-cli upload ./document.pdf
playwright-cli check e12
playwright-cli uncheck e12
playwright-cli snapshot
playwright-cli eval "document.title"
playwright-cli eval "el => el.textContent" e5
# get element id, class, or any attribute not visible in the snapshot
playwright-cli eval "el => el.id" e5
playwright-cli eval "el => el.getAttribute('data-testid')" e5
playwright-cli dialog-accept
playwright-cli dialog-accept "confirmation text"
playwright-cli dialog-dismiss
playwright-cli resize 1920 1080
playwright-cli close
```

### Navigation

```bash
playwright-cli go-back
playwright-cli go-forward
playwright-cli reload
```

### Keyboard

```bash
playwright-cli press Enter
playwright-cli press ArrowDown
playwright-cli keydown Shift
playwright-cli keyup Shift
```

### Mouse

```bash
playwright-cli mousemove 150 300
playwright-cli mousedown
playwright-cli mousedown right
playwright-cli mouseup
playwright-cli mouseup right
playwright-cli mousewheel 0 100
```

### Save as

```bash
playwright-cli screenshot
playwright-cli screenshot e5
playwright-cli screenshot --filename=page.png
playwright-cli pdf --filename=page.pdf
```

### Tabs

```bash
playwright-cli tab-list
playwright-cli tab-new
playwright-cli tab-new https://example.com/page
playwright-cli tab-close
playwright-cli tab-close 2
playwright-cli tab-select 0
```

### Storage

```bash
playwright-cli state-save
playwright-cli state-save auth.json
playwright-cli state-load auth.json

# Cookies
playwright-cli cookie-list
playwright-cli cookie-list --domain=example.com
playwright-cli cookie-get session_id
playwright-cli cookie-set session_id abc123
playwright-cli cookie-set session_id abc123 --domain=example.com --httpOnly --secure
playwright-cli cookie-delete session_id
playwright-cli cookie-clear

# LocalStorage
playwright-cli localstorage-list
playwright-cli localstorage-get theme
playwright-cli localstorage-set theme dark
playwright-cli localstorage-delete theme
playwright-cli localstorage-clear

# SessionStorage
playwright-cli sessionstorage-list
playwright-cli sessionstorage-get step
playwright-cli sessionstorage-set step 3
playwright-cli sessionstorage-delete step
playwright-cli sessionstorage-clear
```

### Network

```bash
playwright-cli route "**/*.jpg" --status=404
playwright-cli route "https://api.example.com/**" --body='{"mock": true}'
playwright-cli route-list
playwright-cli unroute "**/*.jpg"
playwright-cli unroute
```

### DevTools

```bash
playwright-cli console
playwright-cli console warning
playwright-cli network
playwright-cli run-code "async page => await page.context().grantPermissions(['geolocation'])"
playwright-cli run-code --filename=script.js
playwright-cli tracing-start
playwright-cli tracing-stop
playwright-cli video-start video.webm
playwright-cli video-chapter "Chapter Title" --description="Details" --duration=2000
playwright-cli video-stop
```

## Raw output

The global `--raw` option strips page status, generated code, and snapshot sections from the output, returning only the result value. Use it to pipe command output into other tools. Commands that don't produce output return nothing.

```bash
playwright-cli --raw eval "JSON.stringify(performance.timing)" | jq '.loadEventEnd - .navigationStart'
playwright-cli --raw eval "JSON.stringify([...document.querySelectorAll('a')].map(a => a.href))" > links.json
playwright-cli --raw snapshot > before.yml
playwright-cli click e5
playwright-cli --raw snapshot > after.yml
diff before.yml after.yml
TOKEN=$(playwright-cli --raw cookie-get session_id)
playwright-cli --raw localstorage-get theme
```

## Open parameters
```bash
# Use specific browser when creating session
playwright-cli open --browser=chrome
playwright-cli open --browser=firefox
playwright-cli open --browser=webkit
playwright-cli open --browser=msedge

# Use persistent profile (by default profile is in-memory)
playwright-cli open --persistent
# Use persistent profile with custom directory
playwright-cli open --profile=/path/to/profile

# Connect to browser via extension
playwright-cli attach --extension

# Connect to a running Chrome or Edge by channel name
playwright-cli attach --cdp=chrome
playwright-cli attach --cdp=msedge

# Connect to a running browser via CDP endpoint
playwright-cli attach --cdp=http://localhost:9222

# Start with config file
playwright-cli open --config=my-config.json

# Close the browser
playwright-cli close
# Delete user data for the default session
playwright-cli delete-data
```

## Snapshots

After each command, playwright-cli provides a snapshot of the current browser state.

```bash
> playwright-cli goto https://example.com
### Page
- Page URL: https://example.com/
- Page Title: Example Domain
### Snapshot
[Snapshot](.playwright-cli/page-2026-02-14T19-22-42-679Z.yml)
```

You can also take a snapshot on demand using `playwright-cli snapshot` command. All the options below can be combined as needed.

```bash
# default - save to a file with timestamp-based name
playwright-cli snapshot

# save to file, use when snapshot is a part of the workflow result
playwright-cli snapshot --filename=after-click.yaml

# snapshot an element instead of the whole page
playwright-cli snapshot "#main"

# limit snapshot depth for efficiency, take a partial snapshot afterwards
playwright-cli snapshot --depth=4
playwright-cli snapshot e34
```

## Targeting elements

By default, use refs from the snapshot to interact with page elements.

```bash
# get snapshot with refs
playwright-cli snapshot

# interact using a ref
playwright-cli click e15
```

You can also use css selectors or Playwright locators.

```bash
# css selector
playwright-cli click "#main > button.submit"

# role locator
playwright-cli click "getByRole('button', { name: 'Submit' })"

# test id
playwright-cli click "getByTestId('submit-button')"
```

## Browser Sessions

```bash
# create new browser session named "mysession" with persistent profile
playwright-cli -s=mysession open example.com --persistent
# same with manually specified profile directory (use when requested explicitly)
playwright-cli -s=mysession open example.com --profile=/path/to/profile
playwright-cli -s=mysession click e6
playwright-cli -s=mysession close  # stop a named browser
playwright-cli -s=mysession delete-data  # delete user data for persistent session

playwright-cli list
# Close all browsers
playwright-cli close-all
# Forcefully kill all browser processes
playwright-cli kill-all
```

## Installation

If global `playwright-cli` command is not available, try a local version via `npx playwright-cli`:

```bash
npx --no-install playwright-cli --version
```

When local version is available, use `npx playwright-cli` in all commands. Otherwise, install `playwright-cli` as a global command:

```bash
npm install -g @playwright/cli@latest
```

## Example: Form submission

```bash
playwright-cli open https://example.com/form
playwright-cli snapshot

playwright-cli fill e1 "user@example.com"
playwright-cli fill e2 "password123"
playwright-cli click e3
playwright-cli snapshot
playwright-cli close
```

## Example: Multi-tab workflow

```bash
playwright-cli open https://example.com
playwright-cli tab-new https://example.com/other
playwright-cli tab-list
playwright-cli tab-select 0
playwright-cli snapshot
playwright-cli close
```

## Example: Debugging with DevTools

```bash
playwright-cli open https://example.com
playwright-cli click e4
playwright-cli fill e7 "test"
playwright-cli console
playwright-cli network
playwright-cli close
```

```bash
playwright-cli open https://example.com
playwright-cli tracing-start
playwright-cli click e4
playwright-cli fill e7 "test"
playwright-cli tracing-stop
playwright-cli close
```

2. Key Technical Concepts:
   - AnimeJS v4 `onScroll` with `sync: 0.5` smoothing, threshold callbacks
   - AnimeJS threshold syntax: `'<container> <target>'` (container edge first), confirmed via official docs
   - Build-then-link pattern: `createTimeline({ autoplay: false })` then `observer.link(tl)` — linking an empty timeline scrubs nothing
   - Vue 3 `<transition>` with CSS-named transitions vs JS hooks (JS hooks broke Firefox)
   - SVG viewBox scaling: text font-size in user units scales with SVG render width
   - `prefers-reduced-motion` accessibility gating

3. Files and Code Sections:

   - `projects/cpuchip.net/src/animation/lcars-motion.ts`
     - Core animation primitives. Final state of `diagramScroll`:
     ```ts
     export function diagramScroll(el: HTMLElement) {
       return onScroll({
         target: el,
         sync: 0.5,
         enter: 'center top',
         leave: (observer) => {
           const target = observer.target as HTMLElement | null
           const containerHeight = observer.container?.height ?? window.innerHeight
           const targetHeight = target?.offsetHeight ?? 0
           return targetHeight > containerHeight / 2 ? 'bottom bottom' : 'top top'
         },
       })
     }
     ```
     - Also contains `drawDirective` (v-draw for section bars), `revealSections(root)` (H2 fade-up via IntersectionObserver), `revealDirective` (v-reveal), `powerOn(root)` (LCARS boot stagger)

   - `projects/cpuchip.net/src/styles/lcars.css`
     - Removed `html, body { height: 100% }` pin (was making body the scroll container)
     - CSS-based view transitions:
     ```css
     .view-enter-active {
       transition: opacity 0.34s cubic-bezier(0.165, 0.84, 0.44, 1),
                   transform 0.34s cubic-bezier(0.165, 0.84, 0.44, 1);
     }
     .view-leave-active { transition: opacity 0.16s cubic-bezier(0.165, 0.84, 0.44, 1); }
     .view-enter-from { opacity: 0; transform: translateY(12px); }
     ```
     - Updated `--topbar-height: 44px`, `--elbow-radius: 24px`, `.lcars-cap` height 24px

4. Errors and fixes:

Then user pushed back ("maybe it wasn't backwards?") — I read official docs which confirmed my second reading. User was correct to push for documentation verification.
   - **`createTimeline({ autoplay: observer })` linking to empty timeline**: Fixed by building timeline first, then `observer.link(tl)` after `.add()` calls.
   - **Body scroll trap**: `html, body { height: 100% }` made body the scroll container instead of document. Removed the height pin.
   - **`leave: 'bottom bottom'` inverted on phone portrait**: When H < vh/2, distance is negative, AnimeJS silently clamps to 0. Fixed with adaptive callback.
   - **Firefox crash on view transitions**: JS `viewEnter`/`viewLeave` hooks raced with AnimeJS DOM cleanup before Vue's afterLeave. Fixed by reverting to CSS-named transitions.
   - **Edge cache issue masquerading as code bug**: Earlier "no animation" reports were Edge serving stale cached JS. Browser update flushed it.

Base directory for this skill: C:\Users\cpuch\Documents\code\stuffleberry\scripture-study\.claude\skills\script-refinement

# Script Refinement

A teaching script — Episode for a YouTube series, sacrament talk, lesson, anything where Michael's voice will be heard by an audience — needs more refinement than a study document. The audience can't see the scratch file. The voice tics that pass in a study scream in a video. The fact errors that are private in a personal study go public in a script.

This skill is the workflow we ran on Episode 1 of *Beyond the Prompt*, six drafts deep, after Michael caught patterns one at a time. Naming the passes explicitly means future scripts don't have to rediscover them.

## Why this exists

The 2026-05-21 Episode 1 session ran like this:

| Draft | Pass | What it caught |
|---|---|---|
| 1 | Initial | First draft from scratch + sources |
| 2 | Voice rewrite | 8 "It's not X, it's Y" pivots; cut-list phrases; em-dash density |
| 3 | Meta-narration sweep | 7 places where the script told the listener what was coming before saying it |
| 4 | Partnership voicing | 6 places where AI was framed adversarially; fabricated "yelling at the model" failure beat replaced with real failure modes from chat-history audit |
| 5 | Clarity pass | 4 pronoun-antecedent gaps ("the work," "the evidence," etc.) |
| 6 | Fact-check | 2 factual errors in external citations; verified all scriptures verbatim |

Six drafts is fine for a flagship episode. Six drafts on every episode is not sustainable. The fix is not "be smarter on draft 1" — it's running the known passes as discrete, named phases so they can be applied systematically.

## The principle

**Catch each class of error in a dedicated pass.** Mixing voice cleanup with fact-checking with clarity adjustments means each pass is shallow. A dedicated voice pass reads the whole document with only voice in mind, and finds 8 instances of a pattern instead of 2. The phased approach is slower per pass and faster overall.

## The hard gate (before refinement begins)

Before any refinement pass starts, the draft must have:

1. **A binding question** — the specific question the script answers, written somewhere (header, scratch file, or comment). "Why does AI feel like a threat to senior engineers — and what's the durable thing it can't take?" is a binding question. "AI and gospel" is a topic, not a binding question.
2. **A provenance file** — `teaching/.scratch/{slug}/main.md` (or equivalent) that captures: verified quotes with their sources, the Ben Test calibration for every claim about practice, the visual plan, and any references being pulled from.
3. **The source materials read this session** — not just listed. If pulling from a video transcript, read the transcript. If pulling from a prior study, read the study.

If the binding question and provenance file aren't both present, the work isn't ready for refinement — it's ready for outlining.

## The phases

### Phase 0 — Source curation and first draft

**Audit the sources before drafting.** This is the lesson from Episode 1: the older AI-generated source documents that fed into the script were written by a less-refined model. Pulling from them propagated their voice problems into the first draft.

- For each source document: read it. Note voice problems, fabricated quotes, or claims that don't match Michael's lived experience. Flag these in the scratch file so they don't slip into the script.
- **Run external fact-checks BEFORE drafting.** Every quote that will appear in the script should be verified verbatim via `WebFetch` / `WebSearch` (or `Read` against local files for scriptures). Pull the verified quote into the scratch file. The first draft now has clean citations — fact-check phase later becomes a sanity check, not a structural rewrite.
- **Load the voice skills.** Read [`voice-michael`](../voice-michael/SKILL.md) and the cut-list in [`study/yt/voice-analysis-ai-vs-michael.md`](../../../study/yt/voice-analysis-ai-vs-michael.md) BEFORE drafting. The first draft should already be in Michael's voice. Doing the voice work after drafting is 5× more expensive.
- Write the first draft. Mark it `draft 1` in the header.

Exit criterion: a complete draft exists; every external quote is verified; the scratch file has provenance for every claim.

### Phase 1 — Voice rewrite

Read the whole draft once with **only the voice cut-list in mind**. Don't fix clarity, don't check facts. Just voice.

- **"It's not X, it's Y" pivots** — the stubborn pattern. Hunt them down explicitly. Each one becomes a direct assertion or autobiographical statement.
- **Em-dash budget** — one per paragraph max (bibliographic citation dashes don't count). Re-punctuate offenders.
- **Cut list** — "Let that land," "Sit with that," "Here's the thing," "This matters because," "Read that again," "That's not nothing," "That changes everything," "stops me cold." Delete or rephrase every instance.
- **Therefore/But, not "and then."** Section and paragraph transitions connect by causation or disruption, not by sequence ("next," "also," "the first thing… the second thing").
- **Closing refrain check.** The last paragraph carries the close. Don't restate the thesis as a one-liner.

Mark the draft `draft 2 — voice rewrite`. Voice-audit section at the bottom lists what was caught.

Exit criterion: zero instances of cut-list phrases; em-dash budget respected; explicit voice-audit notes.

### Phase 2 — Meta-narration sweep

Read with **only meta-narration in mind**. This catches the subtler "telling the listener what's coming before saying it" pattern.

- **Telling-then-saying** — *"What I want to tell you next is..."* followed by the thing. Just say the thing.
- **Section-open announcements** — *"In this section I'll cover..."*. The section header already does this; cut the announcement.
- **Section-end teasers** — *"What comes next is..."* at the end of section N. Trust the next section to open with its content.
- **Series teasers that describe future episode internal structure** — naming Episode 2's topic is fine; describing Episode 2's beats is overreach.

Mark `draft 3 — meta-narration sweep`.

Exit criterion: every section opens with its content, every section closes on its own point.

### Phase 3 — Partnership voicing (when AI is the subject)

**Load [`voice-michael`](../voice-michael/SKILL.md)**. Run its 7-point checklist on every passage where AI is mentioned.

- **Anger check** — any line with Michael yelling, fighting, frustrated-at-AI, "janitor cleaning up after a toddler" = fabrication. Replace with real failure modes (tools breaking, session limits, his own shorthand confusing the model).
- **Pronoun check** — *"I directed AI"* / *"AI executed for me"* → usually *"we worked it together"* is closer.
- **Apology vector** — when something went wrong in the narration, take some responsibility for ambiguity (his actual pattern from chat history).
- **Praise check** — when the model did well, acknowledge it. Michael does this naturally in chat; ghostwritten drafts often skip it.
- **Adversarial framing** — *"AI cannot take from you"* → *"None of it can be taken from you. AI commoditises the previous version of what you did."* Removes AI-as-thief framing.

Mark `draft 4 — partnership voicing`. Voice-audit section names each adjustment with rationale.

Exit criterion: zero anger toward the model; partnership pronouns where collaboration is described; no adversarial framing of AI.

### Phase 4 — Clarity pass

Read each ambiguous phrase as a **cold reader** — someone landing on the page without context. Hunt antecedents.

- **Pronouns** — *"it"* / *"this"* / *"that"* — does the antecedent live in the previous sentence? If across a section break, name it.
- **Generic nouns** — *"the work"* / *"the evidence"* / *"the answer"* — needs a qualifier. *"The work you do is more valuable than the work you used to do"* → *"The work that comes out of the partnership is more valuable than the work you used to do alone."*
- **Cross-section references** — *"calls it the X"* at the start of section 2 referring to a noun in section 1 — the listener has lost it. Name the antecedent.

Mark `draft 5 — clarity pass`.

Exit criterion: every pronoun and generic noun has a clear antecedent within the current section or is explicitly qualified.

### Phase 5 — Fact-check pass

Load [`source-verification`](../source-verification/SKILL.md). Verify every:

- **Scripture citation** — read the actual chapter file. Numbers (verse counts, chapter numbers) verified.
- **External quote** — `WebFetch` the original source. Quoted exactly? Article title correct? Author confirmed?
- **Numbers, dates, biographical claims** — every count traces to a tool call this session.
- **Temporal language** — *"last year"* / *"this year"* / *"in March"* — verify against actual dates of cited sources.

Update the source-verification table at the bottom of the script to reflect verification status per row.

Mark `draft 6 — fact-check pass`.

Exit criterion: every claim with quotation marks has a `Read` or `WebFetch` from this session backing it; every number traces to a source; the source-verification table is current.

### Phase 6 — Ship

- **Update status line** in the script frontmatter to final draft number + label.
- **Update README** (e.g., `teaching/episodes/README.md`) status table.
- **Commit** with a message naming the final phase, listing the categories of changes.
- **Push** if the work is complete (per project convention).

For the cpuchip.net companion page (if applicable):
- Transform script → presentation markdown (strip `[VISUAL:]` cues, tighten spoken redundancy, embed `<S>` for scripture refs, link out for external sources).
- Build + browser-verify before pushing.
- Per the cpuchip.net CLAUDE.md: journal + active.md + commit + push.

## Invocation

When Michael says *"refine this script"* / *"run the refinement workflow on X"* / *"do a voice pass on Episode N"*, run the phases sequentially from where the script currently is (use the Status line in the script header to determine starting phase). After each phase, report what changed and commit.

When Michael asks for a **single-pass mode** ("just do a clarity pass on Episode 2"), run only that phase. The named phases are independent enough to run individually.

## Single-pass shortcuts (when phase 0 has been done well)

If Phase 0 (source curation + voice-loaded first draft + pre-verified quotes) was done thoroughly, Phases 1–5 collapse from "find and rewrite N instances" to "audit and confirm zero instances." A clean Phase 0 can take the whole script from 6 drafts to 2.

This is the lever: **front-load the work** that catches voice + fact problems before they enter the draft. The downstream passes are cheap when they have nothing to do.

## Related

- [`voice-michael`](../voice-michael/SKILL.md) — the chat-evidence-based voicing patterns. Load before Phase 0 and Phase 3.
- [`source-verification`](../source-verification/SKILL.md) — the read-before-quoting standard. Load before Phase 0 fact-check and Phase 5.
- [`study/yt/voice-analysis-ai-vs-michael.md`](../../../study/yt/voice-analysis-ai-vs-michael.md) — the AI-presentation-voice cut list. Phase 1 reference.
- [`ben-test`](../ben-test/SKILL.md) — claim calibration. Phase 0 reference for the scratch file's claim table.
- `teaching/episodes/01-the-value-shift.md` — the worked example. Six drafts of voice-audit notes preserved at the bottom of the file as a learning artifact.

- **scripts/git-hooks/pre-commit**: Contains `materialize_writes()` function (Batch G.4.3) that drains pending_file_writes via `stewards-cli materialize-writes`. Lines 71-115 are the materializer:
  ```bash
  materialize_writes() {
      if ! container_running; then return 0; fi
      # Find CLI binary
      local cli=""
      for candidate in \
          "${repo_root}/projects/pg-ai-stewards/bin/stewards-cli.exe" \
          ...
      # Check pending rows count
      count=$(... "SELECT count(*) FROM stewards.pending_file_writes WHERE materialized_at IS NULL")
      if [ "$count" = "0" ]; then return 0; fi
      STEWARDS_DSN="..." "$cli" materialize-writes --repo-root "$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel)"
  }
  materialize_writes
  ```

8. Current Work:

Immediately before this summary request, I was investigating the user's question: "the file is queue, but home come it doesn't automatically drop the file to the FS? is that a flag we need to set? or does it happen on an interval?"

I had:
- Confirmed work_item `science-news-weekly--2026-05-22-2353` reached `review` stage with `verified` maturity (completed!)
- Confirmed pending_file_writes row id 66 exists with `target_path = research/science-news-weekly--2026-05-22-2353.md`, `write_mode = create`, `materialized_at = NULL`, `requested_by = auto_materialize_on_verified`
- Recognized this matches known substrate-shape item in .mind/active.md: "materializer-only-on-git-commit cadence (autonomous batches enqueue file writes but don't reach disk until next human commit)"
- Read full scripts/git-hooks/pre-commit which contains `materialize_writes()` function (Batch G.4.3) calling `stewards-cli materialize-writes --repo-root <path>` to drain pending_file_writes
- Was about to answer the user with the precise mechanism

The exact mechanism: NOT a flag, NOT an interval. The materializer is wired to git pre-commit hook. When you `git commit` in the main repo, the hook detects pending rows and calls stewards-cli to drain them. Files materialize BEFORE commit completes but are NOT auto-staged (human choice on what gets versioned per next commit).
